My Tips for Teachers podcast guests and early book reviewers have shared some wonderful tips on some of the more niche aspects of teaching life that I haven't managed to fit into the structure of this book. So, instead of you missing out, I have decided to compile them into a micro-tips special. 
Enjoy! 
1. 
Teach kids to have three pens: one to use, one to lend, one to lose -from Tom Bennett. 

2. 
While we are on pens... encourage students to buy a multi¡pen. Multiple pens lead to multiple problems! Too many op¡portunities for students to 'forget' them, for them to break, to be thrown across the room(!). Multi-pens allow a swift transi¡tion to students correcting their work, rather than scrambling around in their bag/blazer/coat to find their coloured pen ¡from Lindsey Bennett. 

3. 
Assign student roles for supply lessons as it gives them an extra incentive to behave and provides accountability-from Tom Bennett. 

4. 
Take a few minutes each week to call, text or email the parents of one ofyour quieter diligent students to ensure they know they are seen and valued-from Jamie Thom. 

5. 
If you have a new arrival to the class, buddy them up with an¡other kid and ask them to hand out the books for a week or two (assuming they are happy to do so). This helps them feel part of the class and helps them learn the names of their new class¡mates -from Chris Such. 

6. 
From Craig Gouk -make an agreement to curtail the use of the word 'can't'. We create a bank of alternative phrases together and, at the beginning of the year, make them visible in the classroom until they're established as the new norm. For example: 

. 
'I'm finding it difficult to ... ' 

. 
'I need help with ... ' 

. 
'I've tried this, but it's not working ... ' 

. 
'I haven't been able to figure this out yet ... ' 



7. 
If you've got a class that's regularly just a bit too loud, resist the temptation to keep speaking louder to make yourself heard. Try the opposite: consciously lower your volume to just above a whisper for a week or two -from Chris Such. 

8. 
If you complete worked solutions for any tests, activities or questions, keep a digital copy somewhere for future use. The amount of time and energy you save will help massively! ¡from Becky Read. 

9. 
Buy a decent quality, battery-powered pencil sharpener and keep it in your desk. Trust me -you'll wonder how you ever lived without one -from Chris Such. 


10. 
Glue in worksheets for your students. When students are glueing their work in, there is always the potential for off-task behaviour while students await their turn with the glue, or the glue has run out, etc. I find a quiet point in the lesson, usually when students are doing independent work, and walk around glueing them in. (I ask students to fold them in exactly the way I have modelled before I start.) This also provides me with an opportunity to check in with every student in my class while doing so -from Lindsey Bennett. 

11. 
Stick something thin underneath your stapler and it leaves a small gap so the staple is easier to remove -from Charlotte Hawthorne. 

12. 
Start every parents' evening conversation by asking, 'Is there anything you would like to ask or talk about before I get going?' It leads to much more positive and productive conversations ¡from Debbie Breen (my first head of department). 

13. 
Get your students to remind you ofbreak duties -they'll never forget! -from Becky Read. 

14. 
When looking at a student's performance in your subject, don't compare it to their target grade. Compare it to their perfor¡mance in other subjects -from Adam Boxer. 

15. 
Improve your public speaking by standing on the balls ofyour feet, not the heels -from Jamie Thom. 

16. 
Buy a cheap graphics tablet and experiment by teaching from anywhere in the room -from Jake Gordon. 

17. 
To deal with 'table drift', attach little reference stickers to the corners of tables and the wall that line up with each other, for easy adjustment by students before they leave. This was revo¡lutionary for me this year. So much time shifting tables saved! -from David Geater. 

18. 
Keep a box and fill it with nice things -thank you cards from students, Post-its from SLT on learning walks, etc. -it's always great to look at when you've had a tough day and really helps to remind you why you do what you do! -from Jessica Barry. 

19. 
Never be afraid of sharing your own goals with students. If you are working on your questioning, tell them. I find that students respect the fact you want to work on your practice and skills ¡from Richard Tock. 

20. 
Listen to smart people who disagree with you -from me (al¡though I have almost certainly nicked this from somewhere). 

21. 
Ask yourself: what evidence would change your mind? -from Bradley Busch. 

22. 
Learn to accept that nobody really knows what they are doing ¡from Kieran Mackle.

session.
